Moose Pond Acquisition Corp, NCV I is a newly incorporated blank check company, incorporated as a Cayman Islands exempted company, incorporated for the purpose of effecting a merger, stock exchange, asset acquisition, stock purchase, reorganization or similar business combination with one or more businesses, which we refer to throughout this prospectus as our initial business combination.  We have not selected any potential business combination target and have not, nor has anyone on our behalf, initiated any substantive discussions, directly or indirectly, with any potential business combination target.
Our objective is to generate attractive and sustainable long-term returns for our shareholders by identifying compelling opportunities and enhancing long-term value by driving operational and financial improvements once a business combination is made. We will target potential companies that we believe can benefit from our founders’ sector expertise, relationships and public market experience. While we may pursue an initial target business in any stage of its corporate evolution or in any industry, sector, or geographic location, we intend to focus our search on high-growth businesses across the consumer technology and related sectors.
We are an “emerging growth company” and “smaller reporting company” under applicable federal securities laws and will be subject to reduced public company reporting requirements. Investing in our securities involves risks. See “Risk Factors” beginning on page 37. Investors will not be entitled to protections normally afforded to investors in Rule 419 blank check offerings.

This is an initial public offering of our securities. Each unit has an offering price of $10.00 and consists of one Class A ordinary share and one-third of one redeemable warrant. Each whole warrant entitles the holder thereof to purchase one Class A ordinary share at a price of $11.50 per share, subject to adjustment as described herein, and only whole warrants are exercisable. No fractional warrants will be issued upon separation of the units and only whole warrants will trade. The warrants will become exercisable 30 days after the completion of our initial business combination and will expire five years after the completion of our initial business combination or earlier upon redemption or liquidation, as described in this prospectus. Subject to the terms and conditions described in this prospectus, we may redeem the warrants for cash once the warrants become exercisable. We have also granted the underwriter a 45-day option to purchase up to an additional 3,000,000 units to cover over-allotments, if any.
We will provide our public shareholders with the opportunity to redeem all or a portion of their Class A ordinary shares upon the completion of our initial business combination at a per-share price, payable in cash, equal to the aggregate amount then on deposit in the trust account described below calculated as of two business days prior to the completion of our initial business combination, including interest (which interest shall be net of taxes payable), divided by the number of then issued and outstanding Class A ordinary shares that were sold as part of the units in this offering, which we refer to collectively as our public shares, subject to the limitations described herein. If we have not completed our initial business combination within 24 months from the closing of this offering, we will redeem 100% of the public shares at a per-share price, payable in cash, equal to the aggregate amount then on deposit in the trust account, including interest (less up to $100,000 of interest to pay dissolution expenses and which interest shall be net of taxes payable), divided by the number of then issued and outstanding public shares, subject to applicable law and as further described herein.
Our sponsor, Moose Pond NCV I Sponsor LLC, a Cayman Islands limited liability company (which we refer to as our “sponsor” throughout this prospectus), has committed to purchase an aggregate of 4,933,333 warrants (or 5,333,333 warrants if the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised in full) at a price of $1.50 per warrant (representing a purchase price of $7,400,000 in the aggregate or $8,000,000 in the aggregate if the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised in full) in a private placement that will close simultaneously with the closing of this offering. We refer to these warrants throughout this prospectus as the private placement warrants. Each private placement warrant entitles the holder thereof to purchase one Class A ordinary share at $11.50 per share, subject to adjustment as described herein.
Our sponsor currently holds 5,750,000 Class B ordinary shares (which we refer to as “founder shares” as further described herein), up to 750,000 of which are subject to forfeiture by our sponsor depending on the extent to which the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised. The Class B ordinary shares will automatically convert into Class A ordinary shares at the time of our initial business
      combination on a one-for-one basis, subject to adjustment as described herein. In the case that additional Class A ordinary shares, or equity-linked securities (as described herein), are issued or deemed issued in excess of the amounts issued in this offering and related to the closing of our initial business combination, the ratio at which the Class B ordinary shares will convert into Class A ordinary shares will be adjusted (unless the holders of a majority of the issued and outstanding Class B ordinary shares agree to waive such anti-dilution adjustment with respect to any such issuance or deemed issuance) so that the number of Class A ordinary shares issuable upon conversion of all Class B ordinary shares will equal, in the aggregate, 20% of the sum of all Class A ordinary shares issued and outstanding upon the completion of this offering, plus all Class A ordinary shares and equity-linked securities issued or deemed issued in connection with our initial business combination, excluding any shares or equity-linked securities issued, or to be issued, to any seller in the business combination. Prior to our initial business combination, holders of the Class B ordinary shares will have the right to appoint all of our directors and may remove members of the board of directors for any reason. On any other matter submitted to a vote of our shareholders, holders of the Class B ordinary shares and holders of the Class A ordinary shares will vote together as a single class, except as required by law.
Prior to this offering, there has been no public market for our units, Class A ordinary shares or warrants. We intend to apply to list our units on the NASDAQ Capital Market (“NASDAQ”) under the symbol “MOOSU” on or promptly after the date of this prospectus. We cannot guarantee that our securities will be approved for listing on NASDAQ. The Class A ordinary shares and warrants constituting the units will begin separate trading on the 52nd day following the date of this prospectus unless Credit Suisse Securities (USA) LLC informs us of its decision to allow earlier separate trading, subject to our filing Current Reports on Form 8-K with the Securities and Exchange Commission (the “SEC”), containing an audited balance sheet of the company reflecting our receipt of the gross proceeds of this offering and issuing a press release announcing when such separate trading will begin. Once the securities constituting the units begin separate trading, we expect that the Class A ordinary shares and warrants will be listed on NASDAQ under the symbols “MOOS” and “MOOSW,” respectively.

General
Moose Pond Acquisition Corp, NCV I is a newly incorporated blank check company, incorporated as a Cayman corporation, incorporated for the purpose of effecting a merger, stock exchange, asset acquisition, stock purchase, reorganization or similar business combination with one or more businesses. We have not selected any
1
  potential business combination target and have not, nor has anyone on our behalf, initiated any substantive discussions, directly or indirectly, with any potential business combination target.
Our objective is to generate attractive and sustainable long-term returns for our shareholders by identifying compelling opportunities and enhancing long-term value by driving operational and financial improvements once a business combination is made. We will target potential companies that we believe can greatly benefit from our founders’ sector expertise, relationships and public market experience. While we may pursue an initial target business in any stage of its corporate evolution or in any industry or sector, we intend to focus our search on high-growth businesses across consumer technology and related sectors.
Our Company
MPAC was founded by Brian Sharples and G. Cotter Cunningham, two highly credentialed former public company CEOs with proven track records of building disruptive consumer technology companies that have successfully accessed the public market. Our founders bring over 50 years of investing and operating experience and have demonstrated their ability to identify, and successfully execute against, the massive disruptive trends that define today’s consumer technology landscape. MPAC is the result of a multi-decade professional relationship between Sharples and Cunningham and is designed to capitalize on their complementary expertise and relationships. Coupled with their highly regarded reputation across the consumer technology ecosystem, we believe our founders will enjoy a competitive advantage in sourcing propriety opportunities and be viewed as a preferred partner, which will have a favorable impact on our ability to effectuate an attractive combination. We believe their significant operating and growth expertise and a deep understanding of managing public companies will also bring to bear significant long-term value for our shareholders.
In addition, NCV, a leading investment firm focused on early-stage consumer, enterprise and emerging platform opportunities, is a member of our sponsor group.  NCV was founded in 2015 and has since invested in over 55 companies. NCV consists of seven investment and operational professionals and is advised by eight highly credentialed senior advisors, including Sharples and Cunningham, who are also LPs in the funds. MPAC will target opportunities not covered by existing NCV fund strategies and will be highly complementary to the broader NCV platform. Consequently, we will have complete access to, and expect to fully leverage, the relationships, expertise and resources of NCV.
Our Sponsor
Our sponsor is Moose Pond NCV I Sponsor LLC, whose members include Next Coast Ventures, LLC, Next Coast Ventures II, L.P., NCV Entrepreneurs Fund II, L.P., Brian Sharples, our Chairman of the Board of Directors, G. Cotter Cunningham, our Chief Executive Officer, and certain other individuals.
Brian Sharples
Brian Sharples is a seasoned entrepreneur, public company executive and angel investor who has taken two companies public and served as a director on multiple public boards. Sharples has an established record of identifying and executing against disruptive trends, as evidenced by HomeAway, which he co-founded in 2005 and was sold to Expedia in 2015 for $3.9 billion.
Sharples is currently serving on the public boards of GoDaddy (GDDY), Avalara (AVLR), Yelp (YELP) and Ally Financial (ALLY). He also serves on the board of private equity (PE)-backed company RVShare and is an advisor to Next Coast Ventures (Venture Capital) and Tritium Partners (Private Equity). He is also a member of Next Coast Ventures’ Entrepreneurs Council.
Sharples was the chief executive officer of HomeAway, which he founded with Carl Shepherd. Over a 10-year span, he raised over $400 million in private equity funding to build the platform, scale the team and aggressively expand the business around the world. The genesis of HomeAway was a “blank check” commitment to Sharples from Austin Ventures in 2004 for up to $50 million to either start or buy a technology-enabled business. After researching several market opportunities for approximately four months, Sharples settled on trying to disrupt the online vacation rental market by pioneering a global platform for second-home rentals. Recognizing that several entrepreneurs had already started penetrating local markets (such as VRBO in the U.S. and Holiday Rentals in the
2
  U.K.), Sharples and Shepherd decided on a strategy of both buying existing businesses and aggressively building a common platform for organic growth. After its launch in February 2005 and over the next decade, HomeAway became one of the largest and most profitable vacation rental company in the world. HomeAway went public in 2011 and was sold to Expedia four years later for $3.9 billion. The company now operates under the brand VRBO as part of Expedia Group.
Under Sharples’ and Shepherd’s stewardship, HomeAway was active in serving hundreds of charities around the world, offering significant contributions of time and energy to organizations such as Habitat for Humanity. The company was also a leader in providing employment for disabled individuals and had a strong focus on diversity within its management and leadership team.
Prior to HomeAway, Sharples was the president and chief executive officer of IntelliQuest Information Group, a supplier of marketing data and research to Fortune 500 technology companies. During his 10 years with the company, the business was twice recognized as one of the 500 fastest-growing companies in the U.S. An expert in brand strategy, Sharples has advised several major tech brands, including Apple, HP, Microsoft and Dell. IntelliQuest went public in 1996, and he continued on as CEO until the sale of the company in 1999 to Naviant and WPP Group.
Prior to IntelliQuest, Sharples was the founder and director of automotive marketplace iMotors, a company that eventually raised nearly $120 million to build an efficient and safe online marketplace for used cars. Sharples was the initial CEO of the company, but he left to pursue the IntelliQuest opportunity after recruiting an accomplished automotive executive as CEO to replace him. He remained a director until the company was sold to AutoNation in 2000.
Prior to iMotors, Sharples was a consultant at Bain & Co., with a focus on the technology sector.
In financing his ventures, Sharples has worked directly with some of the top venture capital and late-stage private equity funds in the U.S., including Summit Partners, Austin Ventures, Redpoint, TCV, IVP, Tiger Global, Google Ventures, and Trident Capital.
In addition to his current public board roles, Sharples has served on multiple other public boards, including Kayak and RetailMeNot, and served as the chairman of the HomeAway board. He has also been an active angel investor for the past 15 years, with private investments in over 30 companies and board roles in several. Sharples was the recipient of the Ernst & Young National Entrepreneur of the Year Services Award in 2012 for his work at HomeAway.
Sharples holds an MBA from the Stanford Graduate School of Business, where he has lectured on board governance. He also teaches the HomeAway Case Study annually at Harvard Business School.
G. Cotter Cunningham
G. Cotter Cunningham is also a seasoned entrepreneur, public company executive and angel investor who has taken two companies public and served as a director on multiple corporate boards. Cunningham was previously Chairman, Founder and CEO at RetailMeNot, which he built after receiving a $30 million “blank check” from Austin Ventures in 2009. After an extensive search, he focused on consolidating the online coupon space, where he proceeded to acquire numerous companies over the next 10 years.
RetailMeNot became a leading savings destination that enables brands to engage active shoppers and influence purchase decisions. After founding the company in 2009, Cunningham raised more than $275 million from investors, including Austin Ventures, Norwest Venture Partners, GV, IVP and JP Morgan, before leading the organization to an IPO in July 2013. After several years as a public company, in 2017 he led RetailMeNot through an acquisition by Harland Clarke.
Through these efforts, Cunningham has made a significant impact on the technology business environment in Austin, Texas.
3
  Prior to RetailMeNot, Cunningham served as a CEO-in-Residence for Austin Ventures. Cunningham also was the senior vice president and chief operating officer of Bankrate for seven years, taking the company public. He holds an MBA from Vanderbilt University and is on the board of directors for several private companies and the President’s Austin Innovation Board at the University of Texas. He also currently serves on the Entrepreneurs Council at Next Coast Ventures and is an advisor to Tritium Partners.
Next Coast Ventures
NCV is a leading investment firm focused on early-stage consumer, enterprise and emerging platform opportunities. NCV was founded in 2015 by Thomas Ball and Michael Smerklo, two seasoned investors. Since its founding, the firm has invested in over 55 companies across two funds, NCV I and NCV II. NCV consists of seven investment and operational professionals and is advised by eight highly credentialed senior advisors, including Sharples and Cunningham, who are also LPs in the funds.
NCV is headquartered in Austin, Texas, and is focused on innovation hubs outside of the coastal states. The firm believes there are significant untapped opportunities with highly favorable characteristics in these markets. Over $5 billion has been deployed in early-stage rounds across the markets on which NCV is focused. Approximately 50% of that capital has been deployed across eight key markets, namely, Austin, Denver, Salt Lake City, Minneapolis, Chicago, Atlanta, Detroit and Raleigh. NCV’s focus has allowed it to become highly entrenched and well-respected across the entrepreneurship and venture ecosystem in these geographies, which it believes has led to its ability to capture differentiated, alpha-generating opportunities.
Market Opportunity
We seek to leverage our combined expertise to acquire a platform that is redefining a category through strong innovation and a deep understanding of its customers—in particular GenZ and millennial consumers, who we believe will be the substantial drivers of consumption and growth over the next decade. We believe there are significant opportunities for value creation as technology continues to permeate every facet of our lives and redefine consumer behavior. Ubiquitous connectivity and increasingly powerful mobile devices have led to the growth of connected consumers who are becoming increasingly sophisticated and discerning. In particular, these younger generations of consumers have, since a very young age, grown up with technology as an integral and essential part of their daily lives. These consumers demand transparency, convenience, extraordinary multitouch customer service and superior value from the products and services they consume. They value experiences more than ownership of physical assets, fueling the growth of platforms such as HomeAway and Airbnb, as well as other experiential and nontraditional marketplaces for travel, entertainment, health and wellness, online learning and education, finance, and even shopping through platforms that bypass traditional offline and online retail. In addition, we believe that traditional marketing channels such as TV advertising, print, direct mail and even online search via platforms such as Google have been augmented, disrupted and even replaced in many cases by myriad social channels, connectivity-fueled word-of-mouth marketing and video-based platforms such as YouTube and TikTok, which have captured a significant share of consumer eyeballs and time spent online.
We believe the ability to capture this group of consumers is critical for reasons beyond their sheer spending power. First, these younger generations are the curators of today’s culture and are driving trends upward, heavily influencing how older generations interact with technology. By securing this critical group first, businesses are able to capture a multigenerational opportunity. Moreover, we believe that technological accessibility and globalization are creating greater similarities across younger generations. These consumers are not homogenous by any means, but there is greater shared behavior than with prior generations, which have often been characterized by unequal access to resources and technology. We believe this presents a massive opportunity—by getting it right with GenZs and millennials, businesses are able to capture an outsize, and often global, opportunity.
We also believe the COVID-19 pandemic has affected the opportunity set across consumer technology. We believe the impact of the pandemic has accelerated digital adoption and created significant changes in consumer behavior, a combination that is driving growth across multiple subsectors. The ability to live, work, exercise, learn, get entertained and connect from virtually anywhere has given rise to do-it-yourself online platforms that are growing rapidly and that we believe are here to stay. Multiple target companies with significant long-term potential exist in all of these sectors. We believe the pandemic has also created temporary but meaningful market dislocation in certain sectors which we believe has created near-term value compression presenting an attractive entry point for investors. For example, since the onset of the COVID-19 pandemic, industries such as travel, leisure and live
4
  entertainment have faced drastic reductions in demand, which has led to steep revenue declines and market underperformance. We believe this represents a temporary shock and hold the long-term thesis that a strong recovery will occur in these sectors, with digital platforms driving the majority of the growth post-pandemic. Our team has significant expertise and sourcing advantages in the online travel and leisure sector, and we believe opportunities exist to provide capital to strong technology-led brands that can benefit as their markets recover. These companies can also benefit from a strong balance sheet, our team’s operating expertise and the ability to fuel expansion both organically and via regional acquisitions.
Against this backdrop, numerous consumer-centric platforms have emerged as trusted online destinations for consumers to discover, connect and transact across a variety of consumer sectors. These companies are leveraging both product innovation and a full spectrum of online marketing channels to be significant disruptors in their categories and build share quickly with the very consumers who will influence and drive economic activity for years to come. Several of these companies have achieved the scale and market readiness to become highly compelling assets for public equity investors and have also demonstrated the ability to create significant barriers to entry as they grow, creating the potential for high profitability and long-term growth. Some of these success stories include goods and services marketplaces such as Etsy, Airbnb, Uber, VRBO, Poshmark, Farfetch, Mercado Libre and Upwork, as well as innovative subscription/subscription-like businesses such as Netflix, Peloton, Shopify, Roku, Chewy and GoodRx and disruptive fintech platforms such as Sofi, Robinhood, Square and Greendot. Our investment focus will be on private companies that have built marketplace platforms, subscription services and online strategies that are poised for continued disruption and can be replicated in markets around the world through both organic and inorganic growth.
We also believe certain sectors across consumer technology present interesting consolidation opportunities. Our founders are deeply entrenched across the ecosystem and are well-positioned to combine market leaders or disruptors that together will have the scale and market share to represent a compelling public company with significant post-IPO growth potential. Similar to the strategy employed in building HomeAway and RetailMeNot, we believe we have the opportunity to identify combinations of businesses that provide a platform for capturing significant market share, while leveraging the operating advantages provided by additional scale. These advantages include the ability to hire and retain world-class talent, enhanced negotiation with suppliers, marketing scale and investment in continued innovation and R&D, as well as the opportunity to leverage the public markets for growth capital, creating a significant advantage over smaller and less well-funded competitors. In these situations, our CEO-led management team can provide significant and meaningful value-add to founders we believe will welcome our expertise on integrating the companies and preparing them for a public listing. We also believe that this sourcing strategy will result in proprietary deal flow versus other SPACs that are only focused on a single acquisition.
We also believe there may be several potential domestic/international combinations that will allow us to create a global leader, with a resulting listing on a U.S. stock exchange. Our team has significant experience with acquisitions in virtually every leading EU country, and we believe that many of the available assets overseas can represent a better value than those in the U.S. As such, we intend to leverage our strong connections in Europe, as well as our board, to seek market-leading businesses in Europe that could benefit from a combination with a similar U.S. platform, creating both scale and a springboard for further international growth.
Our Competitive Advantage
Our sponsors share a strategic vision that we believe will allow us to capture outsize and undervalued market opportunities across consumer technology. We are well-positioned to achieve this by executing against a disciplined framework that leverages our competitive advantages, including:
Proprietary sourcing engine leveraging depth and breadth of relationships: We intend to capitalize on the established reputations of Sharples and Cunningham and their deep network across the ecosystem to drive proprietary deal flow. Developed over multiple decades, our founders’ hard-to-replicate relationships with entrepreneurs, investors, venture- and late-stage private equity firms, and operators deeply entrench them across the consumer technology landscape. In addition, many of the senior leaders from companies operated by Sharples and Cunningham have gone on to be founders and/or CEOs of successful consumer internet businesses. We have also assembled an experienced board of operators across travel, fintech, consumer services and software and plan to leverage their networks, experience and vision in developing sourcing targets in both the U.S. and Europe. We also believe we have a competitive advantage sourcing outside of Silicon Valley, especially in Central Texas and Austin,
5
  specifically, which has quickly become one of the leading regions in the world for technology innovation and disruption.
We also believe there is a unique opportunity for our founders to create exclusive deal flow by seeking to combine industry leaders or disruptors that together will have the scale and market share to represent a compelling public company with significant post-IPO growth potential. We plan to further extend this strategy by sourcing outside the U.S. and looking for domestic/international combinations that will allow us to create a global leader.
In addition, NCV will further supplement and broaden our sourcing funnel by directing proprietary deal flow from its extensive network of entrepreneurs, management teams and former executives of public and private companies, venture capitalists and private equity sponsors.
Disciplined and thesis-driven investment framework and due diligence process: Across our founders, board and advisors/sponsors, we have collectively executed over 100 acquisitions and have developed a proven playbook for evaluating opportunities. In our assessment of potential business combination targets, we intend to apply a thesis-driven, rigorous and value-disciplined approach. Both Sharples and Cunningham operated platforms that were profitable from year one, and we will have a strong focus on profit potential over a three- to five-year period following acquisition, while prioritizing the right investments for continued growth. Our focus will be on opportunities that align with our aforementioned market opportunity and demonstrate key business and financial signals.
Our sponsors will be supported by a dedicated MPAC team that will assist with the evaluation and due diligence of potential opportunities. We will also leverage NCV and external relationships to evaluate market sizing, competitive dynamics and consumer sentiments to assess the long-term attractiveness of potential targets. We will perform fundamental valuation analyses and apply a value-disciplined approach that will allow us to anticipate attractive returns on capital for our investors.
Differentiated sponsorship driving favorable transaction dynamics and long-term value: We are a CEO-led team with a proven track record of successfully building consumer technology platforms and leading them into the public market. Our founders will be dedicated long-term partners and plan to remain highly involved at the board level. Based on our combined 15 years of operating public companies, we believe we are well-positioned to guide a company through the necessary measures needed for a publicly traded entity, as well as to deliver extensive operational experience that can enhance the value of our target post-business combination.
As CEOs, both Sharples and Cunningham were considered to be very strong visionaries, brand stewards and operators by both investors and employees. We have a consistent philosophy of surrounding ourselves with the smartest and most capable business leaders, with little tolerance for those who are not strong team players and a focus on those who can listen just as well as they lead. We are experts at building organizations with complementary skills that can execute an aggressive growth strategy, while driving decision-making and operating responsibility to the places in the organization with the best information and ability to execute quickly. We believe in a culture that rewards data-driven decision-making, which includes a deep understanding of customers, competitors, development cycles, prioritization of projects based on ROI, funnel metrics to minimize cost of customer acquisition and world-class product and service delivery that provides high Net Promoter Scores. We believe that the best leaders exhibit humility as a gateway to continuous learning and improvement, while pushing themselves to do their best work each and every day. We also understand from experience the benefits of setting stretch goals for both the company and individuals, with a regular cadence of measurement, improvement and rewards. Additionally, we have significant public experience in audit, compensation, ESG and governance that we believe will be extremely valuable to companies pursuing the SPAC path. We believe this differentiation from other private equity (PE)-led SPACs will resonate with entrepreneurs and will be a significant factor in considering a partner in the public listing process.
As mentioned, we also believe there is a unique opportunity to combine market leaders or disruptors that together will have the scale and market share to represent a compelling public company with significant post-IPO growth potential. Our expertise, reputation and relationships will allow us to assess relative valuations and the most appropriate leadership team to move forward as a public company. We believe there are many market-leading companies that would be compelling potential public company targets. Our resources and expertise, along with the
6
  potential for these target companies to achieve public liquidity greater than what could be achieved on a stand-alone basis, can help facilitate an outcome that these companies may be unable to achieve on their own.
We believe these factors will allow us to be viewed as a preferred partner to potential targets, which would be favorable as we seek to effectuate a business combination.
Our Acquisition Strategy
Our business strategy is to identify and complete our initial business combination with a company or companies that can benefit from our founders’ operational and investment experience. We expect to favor high-growth, disruptive consumer technology companies in large and growing markets with certain industry and business characteristics. These include but are not limited to:
  •
Disruptive product and service strategy: We will seek businesses that are using technology and leveraging innovative approaches to win against traditional companies serving large and compelling consumer markets. In particular, we’ll focus on businesses that have redefined product and service delivery for the next generation of consumers, who will drive significant economic activity in the decade ahead.
  •
Long-term growth potential: We will target companies with a demonstrated ability to disrupt, as evidenced by rapid growth and an ability to transform a market or industry through innovation. Often these companies are those that are smaller and start with fewer resources but enter a market by targeting a certain niche, and then use that success to displace previously dominant competitors as its offering is taken up by the broader market. This provides the potential for long-term growth from both market share gains and expansion of existing product offerings. These companies also typically lower the cost of entry for consumers, which can expand an existing market greatly.
  •
Ability to expand across geographies: We will target companies that have the long-term ability to scale across geographies, either through organic entry or through acquisition. Our team is highly experienced in developing international expansion strategies and building multilingual platforms for rapid integration and managing diverse operations. Geographic expansion is another important long-term growth vector that can help sustain outsize growth over the long term. As a result, we will be initially seeking targets in both the U.S. and Europe and working with all companies to identify long-term geographic expansion opportunities.
  •
World-class management team: We will seek businesses run by strong and experienced leaders who have developed a deep understanding of their industry, though often disruptive companies will be run by young and innovative founders who are learning to scale on the job. Successful disruptive companies face unique challenges that require continuous team adjustments to mitigate risk, manage rapid growth and capitalize on opportunities. Because our team is CEO-led, we have a unique ability to advise existing management and leverage our networks to augment teams with the talent and resources necessary to realize a company’s ultimate potential.
  •
Defensible business model with clear competitive moats: We will seek businesses that have the ability to build competitive moats through a combination of scale and network effects. For example, marketplace businesses such as HomeAway are highly defensible as the ecosystem of buyers and sellers grows. Sellers and suppliers want to sell in the marketplaces with the most potential buyers, and we believe buyers will always favor marketplaces that offer the greatest variety and choice. This “virtuous cycle” makes it difficult for new entrants, who must often expend significant resources to catch up to the scale of the market leader. We believe that several opportunities may have the characteristic of leveraging an initial business combination of market leaders or disruptors to create the scale required to develop a truly defensible position and platform for continued growth.
  •
Recurring/reoccurring revenue streams: We will also seek businesses that have a demonstrated ability to benefit from recurring revenue streams such as subscription services or have significant recurring business from existing customers from annual renewals or repeat business. Recurring revenue from existing customers dramatically lowers the cost of acquisition and provides a basis for substantial margin improvement as a business scales. Our team is highly experienced in subscription services and online
7
    renewal marketing and management, as well as developing service and communication strategies that can maximize repeat business and lower the overall cost of marketing.
  •
Opportunity for operational improvement: The core of our strategy is to find highly successful disruptors that also stand to benefit from both a large capital infusion and operational benefits that leverage the experience of our team. Together with our board of directors, we bring decades of experience and wisdom across finance, operations, strategy, brand development, digital marketing, pricing, product development, engineering, corporate governance, compensation, recruiting, CRM and investor relations. As mentioned above, we may also seek to capitalize on companies that have seen some revenue and value compression from the impact of the COVID-19 pandemic, such as companies related to travel and leisure. Many of these companies have learned to operate more efficiently out of necessity and will be in a strong position to move quickly to capitalize from these operational improvements as their markets recover.
  •
Attractive steady-state margins: We will seek businesses that have a clear path to steady-state margins as the business achieves scale. We believe the best public companies are those that can achieve what’s known as the “rule of 40,” which states that at scale, a company’s revenue growth plus net profit margin should be equal or greater to 40%. Our focus will be on companies that we believe can achieve that objective within a five-year window following acquisition.
Our founders have extensive experience building businesses with these characteristics, as evidenced by HomeAway and RetailMeNot, and are well-positioned to evaluate potential opportunities against these characteristics. Our board also has extensive operational experience and will provide invaluable insight post-combination. Our board includes:
Adam Rogers
Adam Rogers has led a rich career in enterprise SaaS solutions that has spanned over 20 years. He started his career at Ultimate Software as a college intern, eventually serving as CTO and then CEO. As CTO, Rogers and his team created the first enterprise SaaS solution, UltiPro, an award-winning Human Capital Management product that brought to market new advancements like AI, machine learning, predictive and prescriptive analytics, natural language processing and mobile technologies. As CEO, he helped Ultimate Software grow to over 6,000 employees and scale to over $1.4 billion in revenue. He guided an $11 billion take-private deal as well as a $22 billion merger one year later. In his last year as CEO in 2020, Ultimate Software was ranked number two on Fortune’s 100 Best Companies to Work For.
Together with Brian Sharples and G. Cotter Cunningham, Rogers is a member of the Entrepreneurs Council at Next Coast Ventures.
Leah Sweet
Leah Sweet is a respected and accomplished technology and e-commerce industry leader recognized for her ability to increase competitive advantages, customer loyalty, employee engagement and profitable growth as an executive at PayPal and American Express by envisioning, planning and operationalizing strategic transformations.
Sweet is a member of the board of directors of GoDaddy Inc. and BMC Technologies. She has held multiple executive-level positions, including senior vice president at PayPal, where her scope of responsibilities incorporated the duties of chief operating officer and chief customer officer, including complete oversight of product operations, strategy and design. She played an instrumental role in quadrupling PayPal’s stock price and expanding top-tier market positions by successfully leading implementation of a five-year agile product development modernization program that embedded innovation in the company culture, expedited time to market, and provided more-advanced capabilities that solved customer problems.

Carl G. Shepherd is a veteran of the sharing economy. A semi-retired serial internet entrepreneur, Shepherd co-founded HomeAway, one of the first sharing economy-based companies, in 2005. As Chief Strategic and Development Officer (2005-2015) he was the architect of the company’s acquisition strategy, negotiating and closing 22 acquisitions and investments and served on the board of directors until the company’s sale to Expedia, Inc.  
8
  For six years, Shepherd served as the COO and head of corporate development for Hoover’s Online.  An internet powered new entrant into the tired world of business information, Hoover’s developed into a leading source for business information online, culminating in an IPO in 1999 and the eventual sale of the company to Dun & Bradstreet in March 2003.
Shepherd has invested and serves on the board of two privately held travel companies, Turnkey Vacation Rentals and HostelWorld, PLC. He is an active angel investor. He is a frequent speaker at travel industry events such as PhocusWright, WIT, EyeForTravel, the China Travel Daily Conference, HostelWorld Conference, and NOAH.
His career began as a consultant, working for what is now Accenture, and establishing a practice based in the advertising industry.  He later served as CFO of magazine publishers Texas Monthly, Inc. (Austin, Texas) and Hanley Wood, LLC (Washington D.C.). Shepherd holds a Bachelor of Arts degree in Business Administration (Advertising) from Texas Christian University and an MBA (Finance) from the University of Texas at Austin.

Andreas Wiele is a highly experienced and entrepreneurial international media and digital senior executive with an outstanding track-record in many different environments and excellent people, creative and financial skills as well as several highly profitable PE-exits.

During his 20 year-tenure until May 2020 as member of the executive board of Axel Springer SE, Europe’s largest publisher has become the role model for a successful disruptive transition from a traditional print publisher to Europe’s leading digital media company. During this time, Wiele has steered and completed several dozen acquisitions of digital companies of all sizes, and the company completed and successfully exited important co-investments from PE-companies Hellman & Friedman and General Atlantic. Prior to his time at Axel Springer, Wiele was Chief Operating Officer of Gruner+Jahr USA Publishing in New York City from 1994 to 2000. From 1990 until 1994, Wiele served as Publishing Director of Prisma Presse Snc in Paris, France. Wiele started his career as journalist of a large German newspaper. He earned a Ph.D. in law at the University of Salzburg in Austria and holds law degrees from the Universities of Munich, Germany, and Dijon, France.

Initial Business Combination
NASDAQ rules require that our initial business combination must occur with one or more target businesses that together have an aggregate fair market value of at least 80% of the assets held in the trust account (excluding the deferred underwriting commissions and taxes payable on the interest earned on the trust account) at the time of our signing a definitive agreement in connection with our initial business combination. If our board of directors is not able to independently determine the fair market value of the target business or businesses, we will obtain an opinion from an independent investment banking firm which is a member of FINRA or a valuation or appraisal firm with respect to the satisfaction of such criteria. While we consider it unlikely that our board will not be able to make an independent determination of the fair market value of a target business or businesses, it may be unable to do so if the board is less familiar or experienced with the target company’s business, there is a significant amount of uncertainty as to the value of the company’s assets or prospects, including if such company is at an early stage of development, operations or growth, or if the anticipated transaction involves a complex financial analysis or other specialized skills and the board determines that outside expertise would be helpful or necessary in conducting such analysis. Since any opinion, if obtained, would merely state that the fair market value of the target business meets the 80% of assets threshold, unless such opinion includes material information regarding the valuation of a target business or the consideration to be provided, it is not anticipated that copies of such opinion would be distributed to our shareholders. However, if required under applicable law, any proxy statement that we deliver to shareholders and file with the SEC in connection with a proposed transaction will include such opinion.
We anticipate structuring our initial business combination so that the post-transaction company in which our public shareholders own shares will own or acquire 100% of the equity interests or assets of the target business or businesses. We may, however, structure our initial business combination such that the post-transaction company owns or acquires less than 100% of such interests or assets of the target business in order to meet certain objectives of the target management team or shareholders or for other reasons, but we will only complete such business combination if the post-transaction company owns or acquires 50% or more of the outstanding voting securities of the target or otherwise acquires a controlling interest in the target sufficient for it not to be required to register as an investment company under the Investment Company Act of 1940, as amended, or the Investment Company Act. Even if the post-transaction company owns or acquires 50% or more of the voting securities of the target, our shareholders prior to the business combination may collectively own a minority interest in the post-transaction company, depending on valuations ascribed to the target and us in the business combination. For example, we could pursue a transaction in which we issue a substantial number of new shares in exchange for all of the outstanding capital stock, shares or other equity interests of a target. In this case, we would acquire a 100% controlling interest in the target. However, as a result of the issuance of a substantial number of new shares, our shareholders immediately prior to our initial business combination could own less than a majority of our issued and outstanding shares subsequent to our initial business combination. If less than 100% of the equity interests or assets of a target business or businesses are owned or acquired by the post-transaction company, the portion of such business or businesses that is owned or acquired is what will be valued for purposes of the 80% of net assets test. If the business combination involves more than one target business, the 80% of net assets test will be based on the aggregate value of all of the target businesses.
Our Acquisition Process
In evaluating a prospective target business, we expect to conduct a thorough due diligence review that will encompass, among other things, meetings with incumbent management and employees, document reviews, inspection of facilities, as well as a review of financial and other information that will be made available to us. We will also utilize our operational and capital allocation experience in evaluating each prospective business combination.
We are not prohibited from pursuing an initial business combination with a company that is affiliated with our sponsor, directors or officers, or making the acquisition through a joint venture or other form of shared ownership
10
  with our sponsor, directors or officers. In the event we seek to complete an initial business combination with a target that is affiliated with our sponsor, directors or officers, we, or a committee of independent and disinterested directors, would obtain an opinion from an independent investment banking firm that is a member of FINRA or from an independent accounting firm that such an initial business combination is fair to our company from a financial point of view. We are not required to obtain such an opinion in any other context.
Affiliates of NCV and members of our board of directors will directly or indirectly own founder shares and private placement warrants following this offering and, accordingly, may have a conflict of interest in determining whether a particular target business is an appropriate business with which to effectuate our initial business combination. Further, each of our officers and directors may have a conflict of interest with respect to evaluating a particular business combination if the retention or resignation of any such officers or directors were to be included by a target business as a condition to any agreement with respect to our initial business combination.
We currently do not have any specific business combination under consideration. Our officers and directors have neither individually selected nor considered a target business nor have they had any substantive discussions regarding possible target businesses among themselves or with our underwriter or other advisors. NCV is continuously made aware of potential business opportunities, one or more of which we may desire to pursue for a business combination, but we have not (nor has anyone on our behalf) contacted any prospective target business or had any substantive discussions, formal or otherwise, with respect to a business combination transaction with our company. We have not (nor have any of our agents or affiliates) been approached by any candidates (or representative of any candidates) with respect to a possible acquisition transaction with us and we will not consider a business combination with any company that has already been identified to NCV as a suitable acquisition candidate for it, unless NCV, in its sole discretion, declines such potential business combination or makes available to us a co-investment opportunity in accordance with NCV’s applicable existing and future policies and procedures. Additionally, we have not, nor has anyone on our behalf, taken any substantive measure, directly or indirectly, to select or locate any suitable acquisition candidate for us, nor have we engaged or retained any agent or other representative to select or locate any such acquisition candidate.
NCV may manage multiple investment vehicles and raise additional funds and/or successor funds in the future, which may be during the period in which we are seeking our initial business combination. These NCV investment entities may be seeking acquisition opportunities and related financing at any time. We may compete with any one or more of them on any given acquisition opportunity.
Our directors and officers are not required to commit any specified amount of time to our affairs, and, accordingly, will have conflicts of interest in allocating management time among various business activities, including identifying potential business combinations and monitoring the related due diligence. See “Risk Factors — Certain of our directors and officers are now, and all of them may in the future become, affiliated with entities engaged in business activities similar to those intended to be conducted by us and, accordingly, may have conflicts of interest in determining to which entity a particular business opportunity should be presented.”
In addition, our officers or directors may be investors, or have other direct or indirect interests, in a business with which we may enter into a business combination agreement and/or in certain funds or other persons that may purchase shares in this offering or that may otherwise purchase our Class A ordinary shares in the public market.
Our officers, directors and any of their respective affiliates may sponsor or form, or, in the case of individuals, serve as a director or officer of, other blank check companies similar to ours during the period in which we are seeking an initial business combination. Any such companies may present additional conflicts of interest in pursuing an acquisition target. However, we do not believe that any such potential conflicts would materially affect our ability to complete our initial business combination.
Corporate Information
We are an “emerging growth company,” as defined in Section 2(a) of the Securities Act of 1933, as amended (the “Securities Act”), as modified by the Jumpstart Our Business Startups Act of 2012 (the “JOBS Act”). As such, we are eligible to take advantage of certain exemptions from various reporting requirements that are applicable to other public companies that are not “emerging growth companies” including, but not limited to, not being required
11
  to comply with the auditor attestation requirements of Section 404 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act of 2002 (the “Sarbanes-Oxley Act”), reduced disclosure obligations regarding executive compensation in our periodic reports and proxy statements, and exemptions from the requirements of holding a non-binding advisory vote on executive compensation and shareholder approval of any golden parachute payments not previously approved. If some investors find our securities less attractive as a result, there may be a less active trading market for our securities and the prices of our securities may be more volatile.
In addition, Section 107 of the JOBS Act also provides that an “emerging growth company” can take advantage of the extended transition period provided in Section 7(a)(2)(B) of the Securities Act for complying with new or revised accounting standards. In other words, an “emerging growth company” can delay the adoption of certain accounting standards until those standards would otherwise apply to private companies. We intend to take advantage of the benefits of this extended transition period.
We will remain an emerging growth company until the earlier of (1) the last day of the fiscal year (a) following the fifth anniversary of the completion of this offering, (b) in which we have total annual gross revenue of at least $1.07 billion (as adjusted for inflation pursuant to SEC rules from time to time), or (c) in which we are deemed to be a large accelerated filer, which means the market value of our Class A ordinary shares that is held by non-affiliates equals or exceeds $700 million as of that year’s second fiscal quarter, and (2) the date on which we have issued more than $1.0 billion in non-convertible debt securities during the prior three-year period. References herein to “emerging growth company” shall have the meaning associated with it in the JOBS Act.
Additionally, we are a “smaller reporting company” as defined in Item 10(f)(1) of Regulation S-K. Smaller reporting companies may take advantage of certain reduced disclosure obligations, including, among other things, providing only two years of audited financial statements. We will remain a smaller reporting company until the last day of the fiscal year in which (1) the market value of our common stock held by non-affiliates equals or exceeds $250 million as of the end of that year’s second fiscal quarter, and (2) our annual revenues equaled or exceeded $100 million during such completed fiscal year or the market value of our common stock held by non-affiliates equals or exceeds $700 million as of the end of that year’s second fiscal quarter.
Exempted companies are Cayman Islands companies wishing to conduct business outside the Cayman Islands and, as such, are exempted from complying with certain provisions of the Companies Act. As an exempted company, we have applied for and expect to receive a tax exemption undertaking from the Cayman Islands Government that, in accordance with Section 6 of the Tax Concessions Act (As Revised) of the Cayman Islands, for a period of 20 years from the date of the undertaking, no law which is enacted in the Cayman Islands imposing any tax to be levied on profits, income, gains or appreciations shall apply to us or our operations and, in addition, that no tax to be levied on profits, income, gains or appreciations or which is in the nature of estate duty or inheritance tax shall be payable (1) on or in respect of our shares, debentures or other obligations or (2) by way of the withholding in whole or in part of a payment of dividend or other distribution of income or capital by us to our shareholders or a payment of principal or interest or other sums due under a debenture or other obligation of us.
We are a Cayman Islands exempted company incorporated on February 5, 2021. Our executive offices are located at 1204 Nueces St., Austin, TX 78701, and our telephone number is (512) 370-2242. Upon completion of this offering, our corporate website address will be www.moosepond.co. Trading commencement and separation
of Class A ordinary shares and
warrants
 

The units will begin trading on or promptly after the date of this prospectus. The Class A ordinary shares and warrants constituting the units will begin separate trading on the 52nd day following the date of this prospectus unless Credit Suisse Securities (USA) LLC informs us of its decision to allow earlier separate trading, subject to our having filed the Current Report on Form 8-K described below and having issued a press release announcing when such separate trading will begin. Once the Class A ordinary shares and warrants commence separate trading, holders will have the option to continue to hold units or separate their units into the component securities. Holders will need to have their brokers contact our transfer agent in order to separate the units into Class A ordinary shares and warrants. No fractional warrants will be issued upon separation of the units and only whole warrants will trade. Accordingly, unless you purchase at least three units, you will not be able to receive or trade a whole warrant.
Additionally, the units will automatically separate into their component parts and will not be traded after completion of our initial business combination.
Separate trading of the Class A ordinary
shares and warrants is prohibited
until we have filed a Current Report
on Form 8-K
 


In no event will the Class A ordinary shares and warrants be traded separately until we have filed with the SEC a Current Report on Form 8-K which includes an audited balance sheet of the company reflecting our receipt of the gross proceeds at the closing of this offering. We will file the Current Report on Form 8-K promptly after the closing of this offering. If the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised following the initial filing of such Current Report on Form 8-K, a second or amended Current Report on Form 8-K will be filed to provide updated financial information to reflect the exercise of the underwriter’s over-allotment option.

Exercisability
  Each whole warrant offered in this offering is exercisable to purchase one Class A ordinary share, subject to adjustment as described herein, and only whole warrants are exercisable. No fractional warrants will be issued upon separation of the units and only whole warrants will trade.
    We structured each unit to contain one-third of one redeemable warrant, with each whole warrant exercisable for one Class A ordinary share, as compared to units issued by some other similar blank check companies which contain whole warrants exercisable for one whole share, in order to reduce the dilutive effect of the warrants upon completion of our initial business combination as compared to units that each contain a whole warrant to purchase one whole share, which we believe will make us a more attractive business combination partner for target businesses.

Exercise period
  The warrants will become exercisable 30 days after the completion of our initial business combination, provided that we have an effective registration statement under the Securities Act covering the issuance of the Class A ordinary shares issuable upon exercise of the warrants and a current prospectus relating to them is available and such shares are registered, qualified or exempt from registration under the securities, or blue sky, laws of the state of residence of the holder (or we permit holders to exercise their warrants on a cashless basis under the circumstances specified in the warrant agreement).
    We have agreed that as soon as practicable, but in no event later than 15 business days after the closing of our initial business combination, we will use our commercially reasonable efforts to file with the SEC a post-effective amendment to the registration statement of which this prospectus forms a part or a new registration statement covering the Class A ordinary shares issuable upon exercise of the warrants, and we will use our commercially reasonable efforts to cause such post-effective amendment or registration statement to become effective within 60 business days after the closing of our initial business combination and to maintain the effectiveness of such registration statement and a current prospectus relating to those Class A ordinary shares until the warrants expire or are redeemed, as specified in the warrant agreement; provided that if our Class A ordinary shares are at the time of any exercise of a public warrant not listed on a national securities exchange such that they satisfy the definition of a “covered security” under Section 18(b)(1) of the Securities Act, we may, at our
15
      option, require holders of public warrants who exercise their warrants to do so on a “cashless basis” in accordance with Section 3(a)(9) of the Securities Act and, in the event we so elect, we will not be required to file or maintain in effect a registration statement, but we will use our commercially reasonable efforts to register or qualify the shares under applicable blue sky laws to the extent an exemption is not available. If a registration statement covering the Class A ordinary shares issuable upon exercise of the warrants is not effective by the 60th business day after the closing of our initial business combination, warrant holders may, until such time as there is an effective registration statement and during any period when we will have failed to maintain an effective registration statement, exercise warrants on a “cashless basis” in accordance with Section 3(a)(9) of the Securities Act or another exemption. If that exemption, or another exemption, is not available, holders will not be able to exercise their warrants on a cashless basis.
    The warrants will expire at 5:00 p.m., New York City time, five years after the completion of our initial business combination or earlier upon redemption or liquidation. On the exercise of any warrant, the warrant exercise price will be paid directly to us and not placed in the trust account.
Redemption of warrants when the price
per Class A ordinary share equals or
exceeds $18.00
 

Once the warrants become exercisable, we may redeem the outstanding warrants (except as described herein with respect to the private placement warrants):
•   in whole and not in part;
•   at a price of $0.01 per warrant;
    •   upon a minimum of 30 days’ prior written notice of redemption, which we refer to as the “30-day redemption period”; and
    •    if, and only if, the last reported sale price of our Class A ordinary shares equals or exceeds $18.00 per share (as adjusted for adjustments to the number of shares issuable upon exercise or the exercise price of a warrant as described under the heading “Description of Securities — Redeemable Warrants — Public Shareholders’ Redeemable Warrants — Anti-dilution Adjustments”) for any 20 trading days within a 30 trading day period ending on the third trading day prior to the date on which we send the notice of redemption to the warrant holders.
16
      We will not redeem the warrants unless a registration statement under the Securities Act covering the issuance of the Class A ordinary shares issuable upon exercise of the warrants is then effective and a current prospectus relating to those Class A ordinary shares is available throughout the 30-day redemption period, except if the warrants may be exercised on a cashless basis and such cashless exercise is exempt from registration under the Securities Act. If and when the warrants become redeemable by us, we may exercise our redemption right even if we are unable to register or qualify the underlying securities for sale under all applicable state securities laws.
If we call the warrants for redemption as described above, our management will have the option to require all holders that wish to exercise warrants to do so on a “cashless basis.” In determining whether to require all holders to exercise their warrants on a “cashless basis,” our management will consider, among other factors, our cash position, the number of warrants that are outstanding and the dilutive effect on our shareholders of issuing the maximum number of Class A ordinary shares issuable upon the exercise of our warrants. In such event, each holder would pay the exercise price by surrendering the warrants for that number of Class A ordinary shares equal to the quotient obtained by dividing (x) the product of the number of Class A ordinary shares underlying the warrants, multiplied by the excess of the “fair market value” (defined below) over the exercise price of the warrants by (y) the fair market value. The “fair market value” shall mean the average last reported sale price of the Class A ordinary shares for the 10 trading days ending on the third trading day prior to the date on which the notice of redemption is sent to the holders of warrants. Please see the section entitled “Description of Securities — Redeemable Warrants — Public Shareholders’ Redeemable Warrants” for additional information.
None of the private placement warrants will be redeemable by us so long as they are held by our sponsor or its permitted transferees.
Redemption of warrants when the price
per Class A ordinary share equals or
exceeds $10.00
 

Once the warrants become exercisable, we may redeem the outstanding warrants:
•   in whole and not in part;
•   at a price of $0.10 per warrant upon a minimum of 30 days’ prior written notice of redemption provided that holders will be able to exercise their warrants on a “cashless basis” prior to redemption and receive a number of Class A ordinary shares determined by reference to the table set forth under “Description of Securities — Redeemable Warrants — Public Shareholders’ Redeemable Warrants” based on the redemption date and the “fair market value” of our Class  A ordinary shares (as defined below) except as otherwise described in “Description of Securities — Redeemable Warrants — Public Shareholders’ Redeemable Warrants”;
•   if, and only if, the last reported sale price of our Class A ordinary shares equals or exceeds $10.00 per share (as adjusted and described under “Description of Securities – Warrants – Public Shareholders’ Redeemable Warrants – Anti-dilution Adjustments”) on the trading day prior to the date on which we send the notice of redemption to the warrant holders; and
17
      •   if, and only if, the last reported sale price of our Class A ordinary shares is less than $18.00 per share (as adjusted for adjustments to the number of shares issuable upon exercise or the exercise price of a warrant as described under the heading “Description of Securities — Redeemable Warrants — Public Shareholders’ Warrants  — Anti-dilution Adjustments”) on the trading day prior to the date on which we send the notice of redemption to the warrant holders, the private placement warrants must also be concurrently called for redemption on the same terms as the outstanding public warrants, as described above.
    The “fair market value” of our Class A ordinary shares shall mean the average last reported sale price of our Class A ordinary shares for the 10 trading days immediately following the date on which the notice of redemption is sent to the holders of warrants. We will provide our warrant holders with the final fair market value no later than one business day after the ten trading day period described above ends. In no event will the warrants be exercisable on a “cashless basis” in connection with this redemption feature for more than 0.361 Class A ordinary shares per whole warrant (subject to adjustment). Founder shares
  On February 5, 2021, our sponsor subscribed for an aggregate of 5,750,000 Class B ordinary shares, par value $0.0001 per share, for an aggregate purchase price of $25,000, or approximately $0.004 per share.
    Prior to the initial investment in the company of $25,000 by our sponsor, the company had no assets, tangible or intangible. The purchase price of these founder shares was determined by dividing the amount of cash contributed to us by the number of founder shares issued. Our initial shareholders will collectively own 20% of our issued and outstanding shares after this offering (assuming they do not purchase any units in this offering). If we increase or decrease the size of this offering, we will effect a capitalization or share repurchase or redemption or other appropriate mechanism, as applicable, with respect to our founder shares immediately prior to the consummation of this offering in such amount as to maintain the number of founder shares at 20% of our issued and outstanding ordinary shares upon the consummation of this offering. Up to 750,000 founder shares are subject to forfeiture by our sponsor depending on the extent to which the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised.

    •   our initial shareholders, directors and officers have entered into a letter agreement with us, pursuant to which they have agreed to waive: (1) their redemption rights with respect to any founder shares and public shares held by them, as applicable, in connection with the completion of our initial business combination; (2) their redemption rights with respect to any founder shares and public shares held by them in connection with a shareholder vote to amend our amended and restated memorandum and articles of association (A) to modify the substance or timing of our obligation to allow redemption in connection with our initial business combination or to redeem 100% of our public shares if we do not complete our initial business combination within 24 months from the closing of this offering or (B) with respect to any other provision relating to shareholders’ rights or pre-initial business combination activity; and (3) their rights to liquidating distributions from the trust account with respect to any founder shares they hold if we fail to complete our initial business combination within 24 months from the closing of this offering (although they will be entitled to liquidating distributions from the trust account with respect to any public shares they hold if we fail to complete our initial business combination within the prescribed time frame). If we submit our initial business combination to our public shareholders for a vote, our initial shareholders, directors and officers have agreed to vote any founder shares and any public shares held by them in favor of our initial business combination. As a result, in addition to our initial shareholders’ founder shares, we would need 7,500,001, or 37.50%, of the 20,000,000 public shares sold in this offering to be voted in favor of a transaction (assuming all issued and outstanding shares are voted and the over-allotment option is not exercised) in order to have such initial business combination approved; or 1,250,001, or 6.25%, of the 20,000,000 public shares sold in this offering to be voted in favor of transaction (assuming only the minimum number of shares representing a quorum are voted and the over-allotment option is not exercised) in order to have such initial business combination approved;

    •   the founder shares are entitled to registration rights.
