  80
  MANAGEMENT’S DISCUSSION AND ANALYSIS
OF FINANCIAL CONDITION AND RESULTS OF OPERATIONS
Overview
We are a newly organized blank check company, incorporated as a Cayman Islands exempted company for the purpose of effecting a merger, share exchange, asset acquisition, share purchase, reorganization or similar business combination with one or more businesses. We have not selected any business combination target and we have not, nor has anyone on our behalf, initiated any substantive discussions, directly or indirectly, with any business combination target. We intend to effectuate our initial business combination using cash from the proceeds of this offering and the sale of the private placement warrants, our shares, debt or a combination of cash, shares and debt.
The issuance of additional ordinary shares or preferred shares in a business combination:
  •
may significantly dilute the equity interest of investors in this offering, which dilution would increase if the anti-dilution provisions in the Class B ordinary shares resulted in the issuance of Class A ordinary shares on a greater than one-to-one basis upon conversion of the Class B ordinary shares;
  •
may subordinate the rights of holders of ordinary shares if preferred shares are issued with rights senior to those afforded our ordinary shares;
  •
could cause a change of control if a substantial number of our ordinary shares are issued, which may affect, among other things, our ability to use our net operating loss carry forwards, if any, and could result in the resignation or removal of our present directors and officers;
  •
may have the effect of delaying or preventing a change of control of us by diluting the share ownership or voting rights of a person seeking to obtain control of us; and
  •
may adversely affect prevailing market prices for our units, ordinary shares and/or warrants.
Similarly, if we issue debt or otherwise incur significant indebtedness, it could result in:
  •
default and foreclosure on our assets if our operating revenues after an initial business combination are insufficient to repay our debt obligations;
  •
acceleration of our obligations to repay the indebtedness even if we make all principal and interest payments when due if we breach certain covenants that require the maintenance of certain financial ratios or reserves without a waiver or renegotiation of that covenant;
  •
our immediate payment of all principal and accrued interest, if any, if the debt is payable on demand;
  •
our inability to obtain necessary additional financing if the debt contains covenants restricting our ability to obtain such financing while the debt is outstanding;
  •
our inability to pay dividends on our ordinary shares;
  •
using a substantial portion of our cash flow to pay principal and interest on our debt, which will reduce the funds available for dividends on our ordinary shares if declared, expenses, capital expenditures, acquisitions and other general corporate purposes;
  •
limitations on our flexibility in planning for and reacting to changes in our business and in the industry in which we operate;
  •
increased vulnerability to adverse changes in general economic, industry and competitive conditions and adverse changes in government regulation; and
  •
limitations on our ability to borrow additional amounts for expenses, capital expenditures, acquisitions, debt service requirements, execution of our strategy and other purposes and other disadvantages compared to our competitors who have less debt.
As indicated in the accompanying financial statements, at February 5, 2021 we had no cash, a working capital deficit of $155,000 and deferred offering costs of $162,447. Further, we expect to continue to incur significant costs
81
  in the pursuit of our initial business combination. We cannot assure you that our plans to raise capital or to complete our initial business combination will be successful. These factors, among others, raise substantial doubt about our ability to continue as a going concern.
Results of Operations and Known Trends or Future Events
We have neither engaged in any operations nor generated any revenues to date. Our only activities since inception have been organizational activities and those necessary to prepare for this offering. Following this offering, we will not generate any operating revenues until after completion of our initial business combination. We will generate non-operating income in the form of interest income on cash and cash equivalents after this offering. There has been no significant change in our financial or trading position and no material adverse change has occurred since the date of our audited financial statements. After this offering, we expect to incur increased expenses as a result of being a public company (for legal, financial reporting, accounting and auditing compliance), as well as for due diligence expenses. We expect our expenses to increase substantially after the closing of this offering.
Liquidity and Capital Resources
Our liquidity needs have been satisfied prior to the completion of this offering through receipt of $25,000 from the sale of the founder shares to our sponsor and up to $175,000 in loans from our sponsor under an unsecured promissory note. We estimate that the net proceeds from (1) the sale of the units in this offering, after deducting offering expenses of approximately $1,500,000 and underwriting commissions of $4,000,000 ($4,600,000 if the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised in full) (excluding deferred underwriting commissions of $7,000,000 (or up to $8,050,000 if the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised in full)), and (2) the sale of the private placement warrants for a purchase price of $7,400,000 (or $8,000,000 if the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised in full), will be $201,900,000 (or $231,900,000 if the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised in full). Of this amount, $200,000,000 or $230,000,000 if the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised in full, including $7,000,000 (or up to $8,050,000 if the underwriter’s over-allotment option is exercised in full) in deferred underwriting commissions will be deposited into the trust account. The funds in the trust account will be invested only in U.S. government treasury bills with a maturity of 185 days or less or in money market funds investing solely in U.S. Treasuries. We will disclose in each quarterly and annual report filed with the SEC prior to our initial business combination whether the proceeds deposited in the trust account are invested in U.S. government treasury obligations or money market funds or a combination thereof. The remaining $1,900,000 will not be held in the trust account. In the event that our offering expenses exceed our estimate of $1,500,000 we may fund such excess with funds not to be held in the trust account. In such case, the amount of funds we intend to be held outside the trust account would decrease by a corresponding amount. Conversely, in the event that the offering expenses are less than our estimate of $1,500,000, the amount of funds we intend to be held outside the trust account would increase by a corresponding amount.
We intend to use substantially all of the funds held in the trust account, including any amounts representing interest earned on the trust account (which interest shall be net of taxes payable and excluding deferred underwriting commissions) to complete our initial business combination. We may withdraw interest to pay taxes, if any. Our annual income tax obligations will depend on the amount of interest and other income earned on the amounts held in the trust account. We expect the interest earned on the amount in the trust account will be sufficient to pay our taxes. We expect the only taxes payable by us out of the funds in the trust account will be income and franchise taxes, if any. To the extent that our ordinary shares or debt is used, in whole or in part, as consideration to complete our initial business combination, the remaining proceeds held in the trust account will be used as working capital to finance the operations of the target business or businesses, make other acquisitions and pursue our growth strategies.
Prior to the completion of our initial business combination, we will have available to us $1,900,000 of proceeds held outside the trust account. We will use these funds primarily to identify and evaluate target businesses, perform business due diligence on prospective target businesses, travel to and from the offices, plants or similar locations of prospective target businesses or their representatives or owners, review corporate documents and material agreements of prospective target businesses, structure, negotiate and complete a business combination, and to pay taxes to the extent the interest earned on the trust account is not sufficient to pay our taxes.
In order to fund working capital deficiencies or finance transaction costs in connection with an intended initial business combination, our sponsor or an affiliate of our sponsor or certain of our directors and officers may, but are
82
  not obligated to, loan us funds as may be required. If we complete our initial business combination, we may repay such loaned amounts out of the proceeds of the trust account released to us. Otherwise, such loans may be repaid only out of funds held outside the trust account. In the event that our initial business combination does not close, we may use a portion of the working capital held outside the trust account to repay such loaned amounts but no proceeds from our trust account would be used to repay such loaned amounts. Up to $1,500,000 of such loans may be convertible into warrants at a price of $1.50 per warrant at the option of the lender. The warrants would be identical to the private placement warrants issued to our sponsor. The terms of such loans, if any, have not been determined and no written agreements exist with respect to such loans. We do not expect to seek loans from parties other than our sponsor or an affiliate of our sponsor as we do not believe third parties will be willing to loan such funds and provide a waiver against any and all rights to seek access to funds in our trust account.
We expect our primary liquidity requirements during that period to include approximately $500,000 for legal, accounting, due diligence, travel and other expenses in connection with any business combinations; $250,000 for legal and accounting fees related to regulatory reporting requirements; $160,000 for NASDAQ continued listing fees; $600,000 for office space, administrative and support services; $100,000 as a reserve for liquidation expenses and approximately $290,000 for general working capital that will be used for miscellaneous expenses and reserves net of estimated interest income.
These amounts are estimates and may differ materially from our actual expenses. In addition, we could use a portion of the funds not being placed in trust to pay commitment fees for financing, fees to consultants to assist us with our search for a target business or as a down payment or to fund a “no-shop” provision (a provision designed to keep target businesses from “shopping” around for transactions with other companies or investors on terms more favorable to such target businesses) with respect to a particular proposed business combination, although we do not have any current intention to do so. If we entered into an agreement where we paid for the right to receive exclusivity from a target business, the amount that would be used as a down payment or to fund a “no-shop” provision would be determined based on the terms of the specific business combination and the amount of our available funds at the time. Our forfeiture of such funds (whether as a result of our breach or otherwise) could result in our not having sufficient funds to continue searching for, or conducting due diligence with respect to, prospective target businesses.
We do not believe we will need to raise additional funds following this offering in order to meet the expenditures required for operating our business. However, if our estimates of the costs of identifying a target business, undertaking in-depth due diligence and negotiating an initial business combination are less than the actual amount necessary to do so, we may have insufficient funds available to operate our business prior to our initial business combination. Moreover, we may need to obtain additional financing either to complete our initial business combination or because we become obligated to redeem a significant number of our public shares upon completion of our initial business combination, in which case we may issue additional securities or incur debt in connection with such business combination. If we are unable to complete our initial business combination because we do not have sufficient funds available to us, we will be forced to cease operations and liquidate the trust account.
Controls and Procedures
We are not currently required to maintain an effective system of internal controls as defined by Section 404 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act. We will be required to comply with the internal control reporting requirements of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act for the fiscal year ending December 31, 2022. Only in the event that we are deemed to be a large accelerated filer or an accelerated filer, and no longer qualify as an emerging growth company, will we be required to comply with the independent registered public accounting firm attestation requirement on our internal control over financial reporting. Further, for as long as we remain an emerging growth company, we intend to take advantage of certain exemptions from various reporting requirements that are applicable to other public companies that are not emerging growth companies including, but not limited to, not being required to comply with the independent registered public accounting firm attestation requirement.
Prior to the closing of this offering, we have not completed an assessment, nor have our auditors tested our systems, of internal controls. We expect to assess the internal controls of our target business or businesses prior to the completion of our initial business combination and, if necessary, to implement and test additional controls as we may determine are necessary in order to state that we maintain an effective system of internal controls. A target
83
  business may not be in compliance with the provisions of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act regarding the adequacy of internal controls. Many small and mid-sized target businesses we may consider for our initial business combination may have internal controls that need improvement in areas such as:
  •
staffing for financial, accounting and external reporting areas, including segregation of duties;
  •
reconciliation of accounts;
  •
proper recording of expenses and liabilities in the period to which they relate;
  •
evidence of internal review and approval of accounting transactions;
  •
documentation of processes, assumptions and conclusions underlying significant estimates; and
  •
documentation of accounting policies and procedures.
Because it will take time, management involvement and perhaps outside resources to determine what internal control improvements are necessary for us to meet regulatory requirements and market expectations for our operation of a target business, we may incur significant expenses in meeting our public reporting responsibilities, particularly in the areas of designing, enhancing, or remediating internal and disclosure controls. Doing so effectively may also take longer than we expect, thus increasing our exposure to financial fraud or erroneous financing reporting.
Once our management’s report on internal controls is complete, we will retain our independent auditors to audit and render an opinion on such report when required by Section 404 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act. The independent auditors may identify additional issues concerning a target business’s internal controls while performing their audit of internal control over financial reporting.
Quantitative and Qualitative Disclosures about Market Risk
The net proceeds of this offering and the sale of the private placement warrants held in the trust account will be invested in U.S. government treasury bills with a maturity of 185 days or less or in money market funds investing solely in U.S. Treasuries and meeting certain conditions under Rule 2a-7 under the Investment Company Act. Due to the short-term nature of these investments, we believe there will be no associated material exposure to interest rate risk.

85
  JOBS Act
On April 5, 2012, the JOBS Act was signed into law. The JOBS Act contains provisions that, among other things, relax certain reporting requirements for qualifying public companies. We will qualify as an “emerging growth company” and under the JOBS Act will be allowed to comply with new or revised accounting pronouncements based on the effective date for private (not publicly traded) companies. We are electing to delay the adoption of new or revised accounting standards, and as a result, we may not comply with new or revised accounting standards on the relevant dates on which adoption of such standards is required for non-emerging growth companies. As a result, our financial statements may not be comparable to companies that comply with new or revised accounting pronouncements as of public company effective dates.
Additionally, we are in the process of evaluating the benefits of relying on the other reduced reporting requirements provided by the JOBS Act. Subject to certain conditions set forth in the JOBS Act, if, as an “emerging growth company,” we choose to rely on such exemptions we may not be required to, among other things: (1) provide an auditor’s attestation report on our system of internal controls over financial reporting pursuant to Section 404 of the Sarbanes-Oxley Act; (2) provide all of the compensation disclosure that may be required of non-emerging growth public companies under the Dodd-Frank Wall Street Reform and Consumer Protection Act; (3) comply with any requirement that may be adopted by the PCAOB regarding mandatory audit firm rotation or a supplement to the auditor’s report providing additional information about the audit and the financial statements (auditor discussion and analysis); and (4) disclose certain executive compensation-related items such as the correlation between executive compensation and performance and comparisons of the CEO’s compensation to median employee compensation. These exemptions will apply for a period of five years following the completion of our initial public offering or until we are no longer an “emerging growth company,” whichever is earlier.
  86
  PROPOSED BUSINESS
General
Moose Pond Acquisition Corp, NCV I is a newly incorporated blank check company, incorporated as a Cayman corporation, incorporated for the purpose of effecting a merger, stock exchange, asset acquisition, stock purchase, reorganization or similar business combination with one or more businesses. We have not selected any potential business combination target and have not, nor has anyone on our behalf, initiated any substantive discussions, directly or indirectly, with any potential business combination target.
Our objective is to generate attractive and sustainable long-term returns for our shareholders by identifying compelling opportunities and enhancing long-term value by driving operational and financial improvements once a business combination is made. We will target potential companies that we believe can greatly benefit from our founders’ sector expertise, relationships and public market experience. While we may pursue an initial target business in any stage of its corporate evolution or in any industry or sector, we intend to focus our search on high-growth businesses across consumer technology and related sectors.
Our Company
MPAC was founded by Brian Sharples and G. Cotter Cunningham, two highly credentialed former public company CEOs with proven track records of building disruptive consumer technology companies that have successfully accessed the public market. Our founders bring over 50 years of investing and operating experience and have demonstrated their ability to identify, and successfully execute against, the massive disruptive trends that define today’s consumer technology landscape. MPAC is the result of a multi-decade professional relationship between Sharples and Cunningham and is designed to capitalize on their complementary expertise and relationships. Coupled with their highly regarded reputation across the consumer technology ecosystem, we believe our founders will enjoy a competitive advantage in sourcing propriety opportunities and be viewed as a preferred partner, which will have a favorable impact on our ability to effectuate an attractive combination. We believe their significant operating and growth expertise and a deep understanding of managing public companies will also bring to bear significant long-term value for our shareholders.
In addition, Next Coast Ventures (“NCV”), a leading investment firm focused on early-stage consumer, enterprise and emerging platform opportunities, is a member of our sponsor group.  NCV was founded in 2015 and has since invested in over 55 companies. NCV consists of seven investment and operational professionals and is advised by eight highly credentialed senior advisors, including Sharples and Cunningham, who are also LPs in the funds. MPAC will target opportunities not covered by existing NCV fund strategies and will be highly complementary to the broader NCV platform. Consequently, we will have complete access to, and expect to fully leverage, the relationships, expertise and resources of NCV.
Our Sponsor
Our sponsor is Moose Pond NCV I Sponsor LLC, whose members include Next Coast Ventures, LLC, Next Coast Ventures II, L.P., NCV Entrepreneurs Fund II, L.P., Brian Sharples, our Chairman of the Board of Directors, G. Cotter Cunningham, our Chief Executive Officer, and certain other individuals.
Brian Sharples
Brian Sharples is a seasoned entrepreneur, public company executive and angel investor who has taken two companies public and served as a director on multiple public boards. Sharples has an established record of identifying and executing against disruptive trends, as evidenced by HomeAway, which he co-founded in 2005 and was sold to Expedia in 2015 for $3.9 billion.
Sharples is currently serving on the public boards of GoDaddy (GDDY), Avalara (AVLR), Yelp (YELP) and Ally Financial (ALLY). He also serves on the board of private equity (PE)-backed company RVShare and is an advisor to Next Coast Ventures (Venture Capital) and Tritium Partners (Private Equity). He is also a member of Next Coast Ventures’ Entrepreneurs Council.
87
  Sharples was the chief executive officer of HomeAway, which he founded with Carl Shepherd. Over a 10-year span, he raised over $400 million in private equity funding to build the platform, scale the team and aggressively expand the business around the world. The genesis of HomeAway was a “blank check” commitment to Sharples from Austin Ventures in 2004 for up to $50 million to either start or buy a technology-enabled business. After researching several market opportunities for approximately four months, Sharples settled on trying to disrupt the online vacation rental market by pioneering a global platform for second-home rentals. Recognizing that several entrepreneurs had already started penetrating local markets (such as VRBO in the U.S. and Holiday Rentals in the U.K.), Sharples and Shepherd decided on a strategy of both buying existing businesses and aggressively building a common platform for organic growth. After its launch in February 2005 and over the next decade, HomeAway became one of the largest and most profitable vacation rental company in the world. HomeAway went public in 2011 and was sold to Expedia four years later for $3.9 billion. The company now operates under the brand VRBO as part of Expedia Group.
Under Sharples’ and Shepherd’s stewardship, HomeAway was active in serving hundreds of charities around the world, offering significant contributions of time and energy to organizations such as Habitat for Humanity. The company was also a leader in providing employment for disabled individuals and had a strong focus on diversity within its management and leadership team.
Prior to HomeAway, Sharples was the president and chief executive officer of IntelliQuest Information Group, a supplier of marketing data and research to Fortune 500 technology companies. During his 10 years with the company, the business was twice recognized as one of the 500 fastest-growing companies in the U.S. An expert in brand strategy, Sharples has advised several major tech brands, including Apple, HP, Microsoft and Dell. IntelliQuest went public in 1996, and he continued on as CEO until the sale of the company in 1999 to Naviant and WPP Group.
Prior to IntelliQuest, Sharples was the founder and director of automotive marketplace iMotors, a company that eventually raised nearly $120 million to build an efficient and safe online marketplace for used cars. Sharples was the initial CEO of the company, but he left to pursue the IntelliQuest opportunity after recruiting an accomplished automotive executive as CEO to replace him. He remained a director until the company was sold to AutoNation in 2000.
Prior to iMotors, Sharples was a consultant at Bain & Co., with a focus on the technology sector.
In financing his ventures, Sharples has worked directly with some of the top venture capital and late-stage private equity funds in the U.S., including Summit Partners, Austin Ventures, Redpoint, TCV, IVP, Tiger Global, Google Ventures, and Trident Capital.
In addition to his current public board roles, Sharples has served on multiple other public boards, including Kayak and RetailMeNot, and served as the chairman of the HomeAway board. He has also been an active angel investor for the past 15 years, with private investments in over 30 companies and board roles in several. Sharples was the recipient of the Ernst & Young National Entrepreneur of the Year Services Award in 2012 for his work at HomeAway.
Sharples holds an MBA from the Stanford Graduate School of Business, where he has lectured on board governance. He also teaches the HomeAway Case Study annually at Harvard Business School.
G. Cotter Cunningham
G. Cotter Cunningham is also a seasoned entrepreneur, public company executive and angel investor who has taken two companies public and served as a director on multiple corporate boards. Cunningham was previously Chairman, Founder and CEO at RetailMeNot, which he built after receiving a $30 million “blank check” from Austin Ventures in 2009. After an extensive search, he focused on consolidating the online coupon space, where he proceeded to acquire numerous companies over the next 10 years.
RetailMeNot became a leading savings destination that enables brands to engage active shoppers and influence purchase decisions. After founding the company in 2009, Cunningham raised more than $275 million from
88
  investors, including Austin Ventures, Norwest Venture Partners, GV, IVP and JP Morgan, before leading the organization to an IPO in July 2013. After several years as a public company, in 2017 he led RetailMeNot through an acquisition by Harland Clarke.
Through these efforts, Cunningham has made a significant impact on the technology business environment in Austin, Texas.
Prior to RetailMeNot, Cunningham served as a CEO-in-Residence for Austin Ventures. Cunningham also was the senior vice president and chief operating officer of Bankrate for seven years, taking the company public. He holds an MBA from Vanderbilt University and is on the board of directors for several private companies and the President’s Austin Innovation Board at the University of Texas. He also currently serves on the Entrepreneurs Council at Next Coast Ventures and is an advisor to Tritium Partners.
Next Coast Ventures
NCV is a leading investment firm focused on early-stage consumer, enterprise and emerging platform opportunities. NCV was founded in 2015 by Thomas Ball and Michael Smerklo, two seasoned investors. Since its founding, the firm has invested in over 55 companies across two funds, NCV I and NCV II. NCV consists of seven investment and operational professionals and is advised by eight highly credentialed senior advisors, including Sharples and Cunningham, who are also LPs in the funds.
NCV is headquartered in Austin, Texas, and is focused on innovation hubs outside of the coastal states. The firm believes there are significant untapped opportunities with highly favorable characteristics in these markets. Over $5 billion has been deployed in early-stage rounds across the markets on which NCV is focused. Approximately 50% of that capital has been deployed across eight key markets, namely, Austin, Denver, Salt Lake City, Minneapolis, Chicago, Atlanta, Detroit and Raleigh. NCV’s focus has allowed it to become highly entrenched and well-respected across the entrepreneurship and venture ecosystem in these geographies, which it believes has led to its ability to capture differentiated, alpha-generating opportunities.
Market Opportunity
We seek to leverage our combined expertise to acquire a platform that is redefining a category through strong innovation and a deep understanding of its customers—in particular GenZ and millennial consumers, who we believe will be the substantial drivers of consumption and growth over the next decade. We believe there are significant opportunities for value creation as technology continues to permeate every facet of our lives and redefine consumer behavior. Ubiquitous connectivity and increasingly powerful mobile devices have led to the growth of connected consumers who are becoming increasingly sophisticated and discerning. In particular, these younger generations of consumers have, since a very young age, grown up with technology as an integral and essential part of their daily lives. These consumers demand transparency, convenience, extraordinary multitouch customer service and superior value from the products and services they consume. They value experiences more than ownership of physical assets, fueling the growth of platforms such as HomeAway and Airbnb, as well as other experiential and nontraditional marketplaces for travel, entertainment, health and wellness, online learning and education, finance, and even shopping through platforms that bypass traditional offline and online retail. In addition, we believe that traditional marketing channels such as TV advertising, print, direct mail and even online search via platforms such as Google have been augmented, disrupted and even replaced in many cases by myriad social channels, connectivity-fueled word-of-mouth marketing and video-based platforms such as YouTube and TikTok, which have captured a significant share of consumer eyeballs and time spent online.
We believe the ability to capture this group of consumers is critical for reasons beyond their sheer spending power. First, these younger generations are the curators of today’s culture and are driving trends upward, heavily influencing how older generations interact with technology. By securing this critical group first, businesses are able to capture a multigenerational opportunity. Moreover, we believe that technological accessibility and globalization are creating greater similarities across younger generations. These consumers are not homogenous by any means, but there is greater shared behavior than with prior generations, which have often been characterized by unequal access to resources and technology. We believe this presents a massive opportunity—by getting it right with GenZs and millennials, businesses are able to capture an outsize, and often global, opportunity.
89
  We also believe the COVID-19 pandemic has affected the opportunity set across consumer technology. We believe the impact of the pandemic has accelerated digital adoption and created significant changes in consumer behavior, a combination that is driving growth across multiple subsectors. The ability to live, work, exercise, learn, get entertained and connect from virtually anywhere has given rise to do-it-yourself online platforms that are growing rapidly and that we believe are here to stay. Multiple target companies with significant long-term potential exist in all of these sectors. We believe the pandemic has also created temporary but meaningful market dislocation in certain sectors which we believe has created near-term value compression presenting an attractive entry point for investors. For example, since the onset of the COVID-19 pandemic, industries such as travel, leisure and live entertainment have faced drastic reductions in demand, which has led to steep revenue declines and market underperformance. We believe this represents a temporary shock and hold the long-term thesis that a strong recovery will occur in these sectors, with digital platforms driving the majority of the growth post-pandemic. Our team has significant expertise and sourcing advantages in the online travel and leisure sector, and we believe opportunities exist to provide capital to strong technology-led brands that can benefit as their markets recover. These companies can also benefit from a strong balance sheet, our team’s operating expertise and the ability to fuel expansion both organically and via regional acquisitions.
Against this backdrop, numerous consumer-centric platforms have emerged as trusted online destinations for consumers to discover, connect and transact across a variety of consumer sectors. These companies are leveraging both product innovation and a full spectrum of online marketing channels to be significant disruptors in their categories and build share quickly with the very consumers who will influence and drive economic activity for years to come. Several of these companies have achieved the scale and market readiness to become highly compelling assets for public equity investors and have also demonstrated the ability to create significant barriers to entry as they grow, creating the potential for high profitability and long-term growth. Some of these success stories include goods and services marketplaces such as Etsy, Airbnb, Uber, VRBO, Poshmark, Farfetch, Mercado Libre and Upwork, as well as innovative subscription/subscription-like businesses such as Netflix, Peloton, Shopify, Roku, Chewy and GoodRx and disruptive fintech platforms such as Sofi, Robinhood, Square and Greendot. Our investment focus will be on private companies that have built marketplace platforms, subscription services and online strategies that are poised for continued disruption and can be replicated in markets around the world through both organic and inorganic growth.
We also believe certain sectors across consumer technology present interesting consolidation opportunities. Our founders are deeply entrenched across the ecosystem and are well-positioned to combine market leaders or disruptors that together will have the scale and market share to represent a compelling public company with significant post-IPO growth potential. Similar to the strategy employed in building HomeAway and RetailMeNot, we believe we have the opportunity to identify combinations of businesses that provide a platform for capturing significant market share, while leveraging the operating advantages provided by additional scale. These advantages include the ability to hire and retain world-class talent, enhanced negotiation with suppliers, marketing scale and investment in continued innovation and R&D, as well as the opportunity to leverage the public markets for growth capital, creating a significant advantage over smaller and less well-funded competitors. In these situations, our CEO-led management team can provide significant and meaningful value-add to founders we believe will welcome our expertise on integrating the companies and preparing them for a public listing. We also believe that this sourcing strategy will result in proprietary deal flow versus other SPACs that are only focused on a single acquisition.
We also believe there may be several potential domestic/international combinations that will allow us to create a global leader, with a resulting listing on a U.S. stock exchange. Our team has significant experience with acquisitions in virtually every leading EU country, and we believe that many of the available assets overseas can represent a better value than those in the U.S. As such, we intend to leverage our strong connections in Europe, as well as our board, to seek market-leading businesses in Europe that could benefit from a combination with a similar U.S. platform, creating both scale and a springboard for further international growth.
Our Competitive Advantage
Our sponsors share a strategic vision that we believe will allow us to capture outsize and undervalued market opportunities across consumer technology. We are well-positioned to achieve this by executing against a disciplined framework that leverages our competitive advantages, including:
90
  Proprietary sourcing engine leveraging depth and breadth of relationships: We intend to capitalize on the established reputations of Sharples and Cunningham and their deep network across the ecosystem to drive proprietary deal flow. Developed over multiple decades, our founders’ hard-to-replicate relationships with entrepreneurs, investors, venture- and late-stage private equity firms, and operators deeply entrench them across the consumer technology landscape. In addition, many of the senior leaders from companies operated by Sharples and Cunningham have gone on to be founders and/or CEOs of successful consumer internet businesses. We have also assembled an experienced board of operators across travel, fintech, consumer services and software and plan to leverage their networks, experience and vision in developing sourcing targets in both the U.S. and Europe. We also believe we have a competitive advantage sourcing outside of Silicon Valley, especially in Central Texas and Austin, specifically, which has quickly become one of the leading regions in the world for technology innovation and disruption.
We also believe there is a unique opportunity for our founders to create exclusive deal flow by seeking to combine industry leaders or disruptors that together will have the scale and market share to represent a compelling public company with significant post-IPO growth potential. We plan to further extend this strategy by sourcing outside the U.S. and looking for domestic/international combinations that will allow us to create a global leader.
In addition, NCV will further supplement and broaden our sourcing funnel by directing proprietary deal flow from its extensive network of entrepreneurs, management teams and former executives of public and private companies, venture capitalists and private equity sponsors.
Disciplined and thesis-driven investment framework and due diligence process: Across our founders, board and advisors/sponsors, we have collectively executed over 100 acquisitions and have developed a proven playbook for evaluating opportunities. In our assessment of potential business combination targets, we intend to apply a thesis-driven, rigorous and value-disciplined approach. Both Sharples and Cunningham operated platforms that were profitable from year one, and we will have a strong focus on profit potential over a three- to five-year period following acquisition, while prioritizing the right investments for continued growth. Our focus will be on opportunities that align with our aforementioned market opportunity and demonstrate key business and financial signals.
Our sponsors will be supported by a dedicated MPAC team that will assist with the evaluation and due diligence of potential opportunities. We will also leverage NCV and external relationships to evaluate market sizing, competitive dynamics and consumer sentiments to assess the long-term attractiveness of potential targets. We will perform fundamental valuation analyses and apply a value-disciplined approach that will allow us to anticipate attractive returns on capital for our investors.
Differentiated sponsorship driving favorable transaction dynamics and long-term value: We are a CEO-led team with a proven track record of successfully building consumer technology platforms and leading them into the public market. Our founders will be dedicated long-term partners and plan to remain highly involved at the board level. Based on our combined 15 years of operating public companies, we believe we are well-positioned to guide a company through the necessary measures needed for a publicly traded entity, as well as to deliver extensive operational experience that can enhance the value of our target post-business combination.
As CEOs, both Sharples and Cunningham were considered to be very strong visionaries, brand stewards and operators by both investors and employees. We have a consistent philosophy of surrounding ourselves with the smartest and most capable business leaders, with little tolerance for those who are not strong team players and a focus on those who can listen just as well as they lead. We are experts at building organizations with complementary skills that can execute an aggressive growth strategy, while driving decision-making and operating responsibility to the places in the organization with the best information and ability to execute quickly. We believe in a culture that rewards data-driven decision-making, which includes a deep understanding of customers, competitors, development cycles, prioritization of projects based on ROI, funnel metrics to minimize cost of customer acquisition and world-class product and service delivery that provides high Net Promoter Scores. We believe that the best leaders exhibit humility as a gateway to continuous learning and improvement, while pushing themselves to do their best work each and every day. We also understand from experience the benefits of setting stretch goals for both the company and individuals, with a regular cadence of measurement, improvement and rewards. Additionally, we have significant public experience in audit, compensation, ESG and governance that we believe will be extremely valuable to
91
  companies pursuing the SPAC path. We believe this differentiation from other private equity (PE)-led SPACs will resonate with entrepreneurs and will be a significant factor in considering a partner in the public listing process.
As mentioned, we also believe there is a unique opportunity to combine market leaders or disruptors that together will have the scale and market share to represent a compelling public company with significant post-IPO growth potential. Our expertise, reputation and relationships will allow us to assess relative valuations and the most appropriate leadership team to move forward as a public company. We believe there are many market-leading companies that would be compelling potential public company targets. Our resources and expertise, along with the potential for these target companies to achieve public liquidity greater than what could be achieved on a stand-alone basis, can help facilitate an outcome that these companies may be unable to achieve on their own.
We believe these factors will allow us to be viewed as a preferred partner to potential targets, which would be favorable as we seek to effectuate a business combination.
Our Acquisition Strategy
Our business strategy is to identify and complete our initial business combination with a company or companies that can benefit from our founders’ operational and investment experience. We expect to favor high-growth, disruptive consumer technology companies in large and growing markets with certain industry and business characteristics. These include but are not limited to:
  •
Disruptive product and service strategy: We will seek businesses that are using technology and leveraging innovative approaches to win against traditional companies serving large and compelling consumer markets. In particular, we’ll focus on businesses that have redefined product and service delivery for the next generation of consumers, who will drive significant economic activity in the decade ahead.
  •
Long-term growth potential: We will target companies with a demonstrated ability to disrupt, as evidenced by rapid growth and an ability to transform a market or industry through innovation. Often these companies are those that are smaller and start with fewer resources but enter a market by targeting a certain niche, and then use that success to displace previously dominant competitors as its offering is taken up by the broader market. This provides the potential for long-term growth from both market share gains and expansion of existing product offerings. These companies also typically lower the cost of entry for consumers, which can expand an existing market greatly.
  •
Ability to expand across geographies: We will target companies that have the long-term ability to scale across geographies, either through organic entry or through acquisition. Our team is highly experienced in developing international expansion strategies and building multilingual platforms for rapid integration and managing diverse operations. Geographic expansion is another important long-term growth vector that can help sustain outsize growth over the long term. As a result, we will be initially seeking targets in both the U.S. and Europe and working with all companies to identify long-term geographic expansion opportunities.
  •
World-class management team: We will seek businesses run by strong and experienced leaders who have developed a deep understanding of their industry, though often disruptive companies will be run by young and innovative founders who are learning to scale on the job. Successful disruptive companies face unique challenges that require continuous team adjustments to mitigate risk, manage rapid growth and capitalize on opportunities. Because our team is CEO-led, we have a unique ability to advise existing management and leverage our networks to augment teams with the talent and resources necessary to realize a company’s ultimate potential.
  •
Defensible business model with clear competitive moats: We will seek businesses that have the ability to build competitive moats through a combination of scale and network effects. For example, marketplace businesses such as HomeAway are highly defensible as the ecosystem of buyers and sellers grows. Sellers and suppliers want to sell in the marketplaces with the most potential buyers, and we believe buyers will always favor marketplaces that offer the greatest variety and choice. This “virtuous cycle” makes it difficult for new entrants, who must often expend significant resources to catch up to the scale of the market leader. We believe that several opportunities may have the characteristic of leveraging an
92
    initial business combination of market leaders or disruptors to create the scale required to develop a truly defensible position and platform for continued growth.
  •
Recurring/reoccurring revenue streams: We will also seek businesses that have a demonstrated ability to benefit from recurring revenue streams such as subscription services or have significant recurring business from existing customers from annual renewals or repeat business. Recurring revenue from existing customers dramatically lowers the cost of acquisition and provides a basis for substantial margin improvement as a business scales. Our team is highly experienced in subscription services and online renewal marketing and management, as well as developing service and communication strategies that can maximize repeat business and lower the overall cost of marketing.
  •
Opportunity for operational improvement: The core of our strategy is to find highly successful disruptors that also stand to benefit from both a large capital infusion and operational benefits that leverage the experience of our team. Together with our board of directors, we bring decades of experience and wisdom across finance, operations, strategy, brand development, digital marketing, pricing, product development, engineering, corporate governance, compensation, recruiting, CRM and investor relations. As mentioned above, we may also seek to capitalize on companies that have seen some revenue and value compression from the impact of the COVID-19 pandemic, such as companies related to travel and leisure. Many of these companies have learned to operate more efficiently out of necessity and will be in a strong position to move quickly to capitalize from these operational improvements as their markets recover.
  •
Attractive steady-state margins: We will seek businesses that have a clear path to steady-state margins as the business achieves scale. We believe the best public companies are those that can achieve what’s known as the “rule of 40,” which states that at scale, a company’s revenue growth plus net profit margin should be equal or greater to 40%. Our focus will be on companies that we believe can achieve that objective within a five-year window following acquisition.
Our founders have extensive experience building businesses with these characteristics, as evidenced by HomeAway and RetailMeNot, and are well-positioned to evaluate potential opportunities against these characteristics. Our board also has extensive operational experience and will provide invaluable insight post-combination. Our board includes:

Initial Business Combination
NASDAQ rules require that our initial business combination must occur with one or more target businesses that together have an aggregate fair market value of at least 80% of the assets held in the trust account (excluding the deferred underwriting commissions and taxes payable on the interest earned on the trust account) at the time of our signing a definitive agreement in connection with our initial business combination. If our board of directors is not able to independently determine the fair market value of the target business or businesses, we will obtain an opinion from an independent investment banking firm which is a member of FINRA or a valuation or appraisal firm with respect to the satisfaction of such criteria. While we consider it unlikely that our board will not be able to make an independent determination of the fair market value of a target business or businesses, it may be unable to do so if the board is less familiar or experienced with the target company’s business, there is a significant amount of uncertainty as to the value of the company’s assets or prospects, including if such company is at an early stage of development, operations or growth, or if the anticipated transaction involves a complex financial analysis or other specialized skills and the board determines that outside expertise would be helpful or necessary in conducting such analysis. Since any opinion, if obtained, would merely state that the fair market value of the target business meets the 80% of assets threshold, unless such opinion includes material information regarding the valuation of a target business or the consideration to be provided, it is not anticipated that copies of such opinion would be distributed to our shareholders. However, if required under applicable law, any proxy statement that we deliver to shareholders and file with the SEC in connection with a proposed transaction will include such opinion.
We anticipate structuring our initial business combination so that the post-transaction company in which our public shareholders own shares will own or acquire 100% of the equity interests or assets of the target business or businesses. We may, however, structure our initial business combination such that the post-transaction company owns or acquires less than 100% of such interests or assets of the target business in order to meet certain objectives of the target management team or shareholders or for other reasons, but we will only complete such business combination if the post-transaction company owns or acquires 50% or more of the outstanding voting securities of the target or otherwise acquires a controlling interest in the target sufficient for it not to be required to register as an investment company under the Investment Company Act of 1940, as amended, or the Investment Company Act. Even if the post-transaction company owns or acquires 50% or more of the voting securities of the target, our shareholders prior to the business combination may collectively own a minority interest in the post-transaction company, depending on valuations ascribed to the target and us in the business combination. For example, we could pursue a transaction in which we issue a substantial number of new shares in exchange for all of the outstanding capital stock, shares or other equity interests of a target. In this case, we would acquire a 100% controlling interest in the target. However, as a result of the issuance of a substantial number of new shares, our shareholders immediately prior to our initial business combination could own less than a majority of our issued and outstanding shares subsequent to our initial business combination. If less than 100% of the equity interests or assets of a target business or businesses are owned or acquired by the post-transaction company, the portion of such business or businesses that
95
  is owned or acquired is what will be valued for purposes of the 80% of net assets test. If the business combination involves more than one target business, the 80% of net assets test will be based on the aggregate value of all of the target businesses.
Our Acquisition Process
In evaluating a prospective target business, we expect to conduct a thorough due diligence review that will encompass, among other things, meetings with incumbent management and employees, document reviews, inspection of facilities, as well as a review of financial and other information that will be made available to us. We will also utilize our operational and capital allocation experience in evaluating each prospective business combination.
We are not prohibited from pursuing an initial business combination with a company that is affiliated with our sponsor, directors or officers, or making the acquisition through a joint venture or other form of shared ownership with our sponsor, directors or officers. In the event we seek to complete an initial business combination with a target that is affiliated with our sponsor, directors or officers, we, or a committee of independent and disinterested directors, would obtain an opinion from an independent investment banking firm that is a member of FINRA or from an independent accounting firm that such an initial business combination is fair to our company from a financial point of view. We are not required to obtain such an opinion in any other context.
Affiliates of NCV and members of our board of directors will directly or indirectly own founder shares and private placement warrants following this offering and, accordingly, may have a conflict of interest in determining whether a particular target business is an appropriate business with which to effectuate our initial business combination. Further, each of our officers and directors may have a conflict of interest with respect to evaluating a particular business combination if the retention or resignation of any such officers or directors were to be included by a target business as a condition to any agreement with respect to our initial business combination.
We currently do not have any specific business combination under consideration. Our officers and directors have neither individually selected nor considered a target business nor have they had any substantive discussions regarding possible target businesses among themselves or with our underwriter or other advisors. NCV is continuously made aware of potential business opportunities, one or more of which we may desire to pursue for a business combination, but we have not (nor has anyone on our behalf) contacted any prospective target business or had any substantive discussions, formal or otherwise, with respect to a business combination transaction with our company. We have not (nor have any of our agents or affiliates) been approached by any candidates (or representative of any candidates) with respect to a possible acquisition transaction with us and we will not consider a business combination with any company that has already been identified to NCV as a suitable acquisition candidate for it, unless NCV, in its sole discretion, declines such potential business combination or makes available to us a co-investment opportunity in accordance with NCV’s applicable existing and future policies and procedures. Additionally, we have not, nor has anyone on our behalf, taken any substantive measure, directly or indirectly, to select or locate any suitable acquisition candidate for us, nor have we engaged or retained any agent or other representative to select or locate any such acquisition candidate.
NCV may manage multiple investment vehicles and raise additional funds and/or successor funds in the future, which may be during the period in which we are seeking our initial business combination. These NCV investment entities may be seeking acquisition opportunities and related financing at any time. We may compete with any one or more of them on any given acquisition opportunity.
